- (iii) where neither of those things has occurred, at the end of the period of 5 years beginning with the date of registration.

- (2) The owner of the land must give notice in writing to the Keeper where—

- (a) the landholder’s tenancy of the land is terminated during the period mentioned in [sub-paragraph (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/60/1/2026-03-16)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/60/1/b/2026-03-16)[(iii)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/60/1/b/iii/2026-03-16), or

- (b) there is a reduction in the land comprising the holding during that period.

- (3) Where a landholder’s interest in buying land is, or has been, registered, the landholder may at any time apply under [paragraph 58](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/58/2026-03-16)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/58/1/2026-03-16) to have the interest registered again (with or without modification of the matters specified in the notice of interest).

- (4) The Keeper must remove from the Register any registration of a landholder’s interest in buying land which no longer has effect.

##### 61

- (1) [This paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/61/2026-03-16) applies where—

- (a) a small landholder’s interest in buying the land comprising the landholder’s small landholding has been registered under [paragraph 58](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/58/2026-03-16)[(4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/58/4/2026-03-16)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/58/4/a/2026-03-16), and

- (b) the registration has not ceased to have effect.

- (2) The owner of the land, and any eligible creditor in relation to the land, must, before transferring the land or any part of it to another person, give the landholder notice of any proposal by the owner or (as the case may be) the creditor to make such a transfer.

- (3) But [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/61/2/2026-03-16) does not apply if the transfer is an exempt transfer for the purposes of [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/58/3/a/2026-03-16) (see [paragraph 62](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/2026-03-16)).

- (4) Notice under [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/61/2/2026-03-16) must be given—

- (a) in writing, and

- (b) in accordance with such provision (including provision as to the form of the notice) as the Scottish Ministers may prescribe by regulations.

- (5) An owner or creditor who gives a landholder notice under [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/61/2/2026-03-16) must give a copy of the notice to the Keeper.

- (6) In [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/part/8/2026-03-16), “*eligible creditor*”, in relation to land, means a creditor in a standard security with a right to sell the land under—

- (a) section 20(2) or 23(2) of the Conveyancing and Feudal Reform (Scotland) Act 1970, or

- (b) a warrant granted under section 24(1) of that Act.

##### 62

- (1) A transfer of land is an exempt transfer for the purposes of [paragraph 61](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/61/2026-03-16) if the transfer is or (as the case may be) would be—

- (a) otherwise than for value,

- (b) in implement or pursuance of an order of a court, other than an order under section 24 of the Conveyancing and Feudal Reform (Scotland) Act 1970 or a decree in an action for the division and sale of land,

- (c) between spouses or civil partners in pursuance of an arrangement between them entered into at any time after they have ceased living together,

- (d) between companies in the same group,

- (e) to a statutory undertaker for the purpose of carrying on the undertaking,

- (f) a transfer—

- (i) implementing the compulsory acquisition of land under any enactment,

- (ii) by agreement, of land which could have been acquired compulsorily under any enactment,

- (iii) implementing any right conferred by Part 2 (which provides for the community right to buy) of the Land Reform (Scotland) Act 2003 to buy land,

- (iv) implementing missives for the sale and purchase of land concluded, or an option to acquire land which existed on a date on which no interest in buying the land was registered under [paragraph 58](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/58/2026-03-16),

- (v) which requires, or which but for the provisions of section 14 of the Housing (Scotland) Act 1987 would require, the consent of the Scottish Ministers under subsection (5) or (7) of section 12 of that Act,

- (vi) by a registered social landlord (within the meaning of the Housing (Scotland) Act 2010) in pursuance of the power conferred by section 107 of that Act,

- (vii) vesting the land in a person for the purposes of any enactment relating to sequestration, bankruptcy, winding up or incapacity or to the purposes for which judicial factors may be appointed, or

- (g) a transfer of land in consequence of—

- (i) the assumption or resignation or death of one or more of the partners in a partnership, or

- (ii) the assumption or resignation or death of one or more of the trustees of a trust.

- (2) But, in the case of a transfer mentioned in any of paragraphs [(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/1/a/2026-03-16), [(d)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/1/d/2026-03-16) and [(g)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/1/g/2026-03-16) of [sub-paragraph (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/1/2026-03-16), the transfer is not an exempt transfer for the purposes of [paragraph 61](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/61/2026-03-16) if the transfer—

- (a) is or forms part of a scheme or arrangement or is one of a series of transfers, and

- (b) the main purpose or effect, or one of the main purposes or effects, of the scheme, arrangement or (as the case may be) series is the avoidance of the requirements or consequences of [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/part/8/2026-03-16).

- (3) For the purposes of [sub-paragraph (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/1/2026-03-16)[(d)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/1/d/2026-03-16), companies are in the same group if they are, or are included in a number of, companies which, by virtue of section 170 of the Taxation of Chargeable Gains Act 1992, together form a group for the purposes of sections 171 to 181 of that Act.

- (4) In [sub-paragraph (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/1/2026-03-16)[(e)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/1/e/2026-03-16), “*statutory undertaker*” is to be construed in accordance with section 214 of the Town and Country Planning (Scotland) Act 1997.

- (5) The Scottish Ministers may by regulations modify (any or all of) [sub-paragraphs (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/1/2026-03-16) to [(4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/4/2026-03-16).

- (6) Before laying a draft of a Scottish statutory instrument containing regulations under sub-paragraph (5) before the Scottish Parliament, the Scottish Ministers must consult such persons as they consider appropriate.

##### 63

- (1) [Sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2/2026-03-16) applies where—

- (a) the owner of land comprising a small landholding, or an eligible creditor in relation to the land comprising the holding, gives notice to the small landholder of the holding of a proposal to transfer land, or

- (b) the owner or such a creditor takes steps with a view to the transfer of the land or any part of it and—

- (i) the transfer is a transfer in respect of which notice of a proposal to transfer land is required to be given to the landholder, and

- (ii) such notice has not been given.

- (2) The landholder has the right to buy the land to which the proposed transfer relates (including any interest or rights comprised in the land) from the owner of the land or (as the case may be) the creditor.

- (3) For the purposes of [sub-paragraph (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/1/2026-03-16)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/1/b/2026-03-16), an owner or eligible creditor takes steps with a view to a transfer of land when—

- (a) the land is, by or with the authority of the owner or creditor, advertised or otherwise exposed for sale,

- (b) the owner or the creditor, or a person acting on behalf of the owner or the creditor, enters into negotiations with another person with a view to the transfer of the land, or

- (c) the owner or the creditor, or a person acting on behalf of the owner or the creditor, proceeds further with any proposed transfer of the land which was initiated prior to the date on which the landholder’s interest in buying the land was registered.

- (4) References in [sub-paragraph (3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/3/2026-03-16) to the owner of land include references to a person in whom the land has vested for the purposes of any such enactment as is mentioned in [paragraph 62](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/2026-03-16)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/1/2026-03-16)[(f)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/1/f/2026-03-16)[(vii)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/62/1/f/vii/2026-03-16).

- (5) [Sub-paragraph (6)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/6/2026-03-16) applies where—

- (a) a landholder has a right to buy land under [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2/2026-03-16), and

- (b) despite the existence of that right, the owner or (as the case may be) the creditor transfers the land to a person other than the landholder.

- (6) The landholder has the right to buy the land (including any interests or rights comprised in the land) from the person to whom the land is transferred or is subsequently transferred.

- (7) The Scottish Ministers may by regulations modify [sub-paragraphs (3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/3/2026-03-16) and [(4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/4/2026-03-16).

- (8) Before laying a draft of a Scottish statutory instrument containing regulations under sub-paragraph (7) before the Scottish Parliament, the Scottish Ministers must consult such persons as they consider appropriate.

##### 64

- (1) Where a small landholder has a right to buy land under [paragraph 63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2026-03-16)[(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2/2026-03-16) by virtue of [paragraph 63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2026-03-16)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/1/2026-03-16)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/1/a/2026-03-16), the landholder may proceed in accordance with [paragraph 66](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2026-03-16) to buy the land from the owner of the land or (as the case may be) the eligible creditor provided that notice is given under [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/2/2026-03-16).

- (2) Notice is given under this sub-paragraph if—

- (a) the landholder gives notice to the owner or (as the case may be) the creditor that the landholder intends to buy the land, and

- (b) the notice is given within the period of 28 days beginning with the day on which the landholder is given a notice of a proposal to transfer land.

- (3) Where a landholder has a right to buy under [paragraph 63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2026-03-16)[(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2/2026-03-16) by virtue of [paragraph 63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2026-03-16)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/1/2026-03-16)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/1/b/2026-03-16), the landholder may proceed in accordance with [paragraph 66](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2026-03-16) to buy the land from the owner or (as the case may be) the creditor provided that the landholder gives notice to the owner or, as the case may be, the creditor that the landholder intends to buy the land.

- (4) Where a landholder has a right to buy land under [paragraph 63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2026-03-16)[(6)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/6/2026-03-16), the landholder may proceed in accordance with [paragraph 66](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2026-03-16) to buy the land from the person to whom the land has been transferred or subsequently transferred provided that notice is given under [sub-paragraph (5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/5/2026-03-16).

- (5) Notice is given under this sub-paragraph if—

- (a) the landholder gives notice to that person that the landholder intends to buy the land,

- (b) the notice is given within the period of 3 years beginning with the day on which the land is transferred to that person, and

- (c) the landholder’s tenancy is in force on the date on which the notice is given.

- (6) If, at any time, the landholder does not intend to proceed, in accordance with [paragraph 66](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2026-03-16), to buy the land, the landholder is to give notice of that fact to the person from whom the land would otherwise have been bought.

- (7) The right to buy mentioned in—

- (a) [sub-paragraph (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/1/2026-03-16) is extinguished if the landholder does not give notice in accordance with [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/2/2026-03-16),

- (b) [sub-paragraph (4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/4/2026-03-16) is extinguished if the landholder does not give notice in accordance with [sub-paragraph (5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/5/2026-03-16),

- (c) [sub-paragraph (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/1/2026-03-16), [(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/3/2026-03-16) or [(4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/4/2026-03-16) is extinguished if the landholder gives notice under [sub-paragraph (6)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/6/2026-03-16).

- (8) A landholder giving any notice under [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/2026-03-16) must give a copy of the notice to the Keeper.

- (9) The Scottish Ministers may by regulations make provision for a period within which any notice given by a landholder under sub-paragraph (3) is to be given.

- (10) Regulations under sub-paragraph (9) may modify this paragraph.

##### 65

Where a small landholder’s right to buy land is extinguished under [paragraph 64](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/2026-03-16)[(7)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/7/2026-03-16) or [66](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2026-03-16)[(9)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/9/2026-03-16), the landholder may acquire a subsequent right to buy the same land or any part of it under [paragraph 63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2026-03-16)[(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2/2026-03-16), but only if—

- (a) the period of 12 months beginning with the day on which the right to buy is extinguished has expired, or

- (b) before that period has expired—

- (i) the land is transferred to another person, and

- (ii) that person requires to give notice of a proposal to transfer land in relation to a subsequent transfer.

##### 66

- (1) It is for the small landholder to make the offer to buy in exercise of the landholder’s right to buy under [paragraph 63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2026-03-16).

- (2) The offer is to be at a price—

- (a) agreed between the landholder and the person from whom the land is to be bought (in this Part, “the seller”), or

- (b) where there is no such agreement—

- (i) payable by the landholder in accordance with [paragraph 68](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2026-03-16)[(9)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/9/2026-03-16), or

- (ii) if the price is determined in an appeal under [paragraph 70](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/70/2026-03-16), as is so determined.

- (3) The offer must specify the date of entry and of payment of the price in accordance with [sub-paragraph (4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/4/2026-03-16).

- (4) The date of entry and of payment of the price is to be—

- (a) a date not later than 6 months after the date on which the landholder gave notice under [paragraph 64](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/2026-03-16) of the landholder’s intention to buy,

- (b) where the price payable by the landholder is the subject of an appeal under [paragraph 70](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/70/2026-03-16) which has not, within the period of 4 months beginning with the day on which the landholder gave such notice, been—

- (i) determined, or

- (ii) abandoned following agreement between the landholder and the seller,

a date not later than 2 months after the appeal is so determined or (as the case may be) abandoned, or

- (c) such later date as may be agreed between the landholder and the seller.

- (5) The offer may include such other reasonable conditions as are necessary or expedient to secure the efficient progress and completion of the transfer.

- (6) If the landholder has not, within the period fixed by or agreed under [sub-paragraph (4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/4/2026-03-16), done any of the things mentioned in [sub-paragraph (7)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/7/2026-03-16), the seller may apply to the Land Court for an order under [sub-paragraph (8)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/8/2026-03-16).

- (7) The things are—

- (a) concluding missives with the seller for the sale of the land to the landholder, or

- (b) if the landholder has not so concluded missives, taking all steps which the landholder could reasonably have taken in the time available towards so concluding missives.

- (8) An order under this sub-paragraph may—

- (a) direct the landholder—

- (i) to conclude missives with the seller within such period as may be specified in the order, and

- (ii) to take such remedial action for the purpose of so concluding missives as may be so specified, and

- (b) direct the landholder and seller to incorporate into the missives any term or condition in respect of the sale of the land as may be so specified.

- (9) The right to buy mentioned in [sub-paragraph (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/1/2026-03-16) is extinguished if—

- (a) the landholder fails to comply with an order under [sub-paragraph (8)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/8/2026-03-16), or

- (b) where the seller has not applied for an order under that sub-paragraph, the landholder has not (having regard to the period fixed by or agreed under [sub-paragraph (4)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/4/2026-03-16)) within a reasonable period from the acquiring by the landholder of the right to buy otherwise concluded missives with the seller for the sale of the land to the landholder.

##### 67

- (1) Where the price to be paid for land is not agreed between the seller and the small landholder as mentioned in [paragraph 66](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2026-03-16)[(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2/2026-03-16)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2/a/2026-03-16), the land is, except where [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/67/2/2026-03-16) applies, to be valued by a valuer appointed by agreement between the seller and the landholder or by a person nominated by them.

- (2) This sub-paragraph applies where the land in respect of which the landholder is exercising a right to buy forms part of an estate comprising other land in respect of which any other landholder has given notice under [paragraph 64](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/2026-03-16) of the landholder’s intention to buy.

- (3) Where [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/67/2/2026-03-16) applies, the land mentioned in that sub-paragraph is to be valued by—

- (a) a valuer appointed by agreement between—

- (i) the seller, and

- (ii) at least half of the landholders mentioned in that sub-paragraph, or

- (b) a person nominated by the persons mentioned in [paragraph (a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/67/3/a/2026-03-16)[(i)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/67/3/a/i/2026-03-16) and [(ii)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/67/3/a/ii/2026-03-16).

- (4) Where there is no agreement as to the appointment of a valuer under [sub-paragraph (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/67/1/2026-03-16) or [(3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/67/3/2026-03-16), the valuer is to be appointed by the Land Court or by a person nominated by the Court.

- (5) In [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/part/8/2026-03-16), “*valuer*” includes two valuers with an overseer.

##### 68

- (1) A valuer appointed under [paragraph 67](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/67/2026-03-16) is to assess the value of the land in respect of which a small landholder’s right to buy under [paragraph 63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2026-03-16) is being exercised as at—

- (a) the date of notice under [paragraph 61](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/61/2026-03-16) of the seller’s proposal to transfer the land, or

- (b) where no such notice was given, the date on which the landholder gave notice under [paragraph 64](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/2026-03-16) of the landholder’s intention to buy the land.

- (2) The valuer is to assess the value of the land having regard to the value that would be likely to be agreed between a reasonable seller and buyer of such land—

- (a) assuming that the seller and buyer are, as respects the transaction, willing, and

- (b) where the buyer is a sitting small landholder.

- (3) In assessing the value of the land under [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2/2026-03-16), the valuer is to take account of—

- (a) in so far as a seller and a buyer of the land (assuming that they are, as respects the transaction, willing) would do so, any factor attributable to the known existence of a person who (not being the landholder who is exercising a right to buy the land) would be willing to buy the land at a price higher than other persons because of a characteristic of the land which relates peculiarly to that person’s interest in buying it,

- (b) when the seller would in the normal course of events have been likely to recover vacant possession of the land from the landholder,

- (c) the terms and conditions of any lease of sporting interests affecting the land, and

- (d) any moveable property belonging to the owner of the land which is, by agreement between the landholder and the owner, to be sold with, and valued along with, the land.

- (4) In assessing the value of the land under [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2/2026-03-16), the valuer is to take no account of—

- (a) the absence of the period of time during which the land would, on the open market, be likely to be advertised and exposed for sale,

- (b) any factor attributable to any use of the land which is or would be unlawful,

- (c) any increase in the value of the land resulting from improvements to the extent that the landholder would be entitled to compensation in respect of those improvements upon renouncing the tenancy of the small landholding,

- (d) any increase in the value of the land resulting from the use of any of the land, or changes to the land, for a purpose other than cultivation of the land,

- (e) any reduction in the value of the land—

- (i) as a result of any dilapidation or deterioration of, or damage to, fixed equipment or land caused or permitted by the landholder, or

- (ii) resulting from the use of any of the land, or changes to the land, for a purpose other than cultivation of the land, or

- (f) any fixed equipment owned by the landholder.

- (5) Where land in respect of which the right to buy is being exercised forms part of an estate, the valuer is, in addition to assessing the value of the land under [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2/2026-03-16), to assess the value representing the difference between—

- (a) the value of the estate were the estate being sold by the seller to a person other than the landholder, and

- (b) the value of the remainder of the estate (that is to say, the estate less the land in respect of which the right to buy is being exercised) were the remainder being sold by the seller to such a person.

- (6) Where two or more parts of an estate are being bought in exercise of a right to buy under [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/part/8/2026-03-16)—

- (a) the valuer is to assess—

- (i) the value of each of those parts under [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2/2026-03-16), and

- (ii) the difference between the values mentioned in [paragraphs (a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/5/a/2026-03-16) and [(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/5/b/2026-03-16) of [sub-paragraph (5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/5/2026-03-16),

as at the last date on which notice of intention to buy was given under [paragraph 64](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/64/2026-03-16) in respect of those parts of the estate,

- (b) the valuer may, for the purpose of valuation under [sub-paragraph (5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/5/2026-03-16), apportion to each such part of the estate (or re-apportion if for any reason the sale of any such part does not proceed) such amount representing the reduction in the value of the estate as the valuer considers equitable.

- (7) The Scottish Ministers may issue guidance (either generally or in respect of a particular description of case) for the purposes of valuation under [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2026-03-16).

- (8) An estate is to be treated, for the purposes of [sub-paragraphs (5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/5/2026-03-16) and [(6)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/6/2026-03-16) and [paragraph 69](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/69/2026-03-16), as comprising—

- (a) any land forming part of the estate and which is being bought in exercise of a right to buy under [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/part/8/2026-03-16), and

- (b) any other land forming part of the estate offered for sale by the seller at the same time as the land mentioned in [paragraph (a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/8/a/2026-03-16).

- (9) For the purposes of [paragraph 66](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2026-03-16)[(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2/2026-03-16)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2/b/2026-03-16)[(i)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2/b/i/2026-03-16), the price payable by a landholder is—

- (a) the value assessed under [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2/2026-03-16), or

- (b) where the land forms part of an estate, the greater of the values assessed under—

- (i) that sub-paragraph, and

- (ii) [sub-paragraph (5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/5/2026-03-16).

##### 69

- (1) A valuer appointed under [paragraph 67](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/67/2026-03-16) is—

- (a) to invite the persons mentioned in [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/69/2/2026-03-16) to make written representations about the matters mentioned in [sub-paragraph (3)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/69/3/2026-03-16), and

- (b) to have regard to any such representations.

- (2) The persons are—

- (a) the seller and the small landholder to whom the assessment under [paragraph 68](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2026-03-16) relates, and

- (b) where the land to which the assessment relates forms part of an estate, any other person the valuer considers to have an interest in the estate.

- (3) The matters are—

- (a) the valuation of the land under [paragraph 68](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2026-03-16), and

- (b) where the land forms part of an estate, any valuation of the estate (and any apportionment of a reduction in the value of the estate) under that paragraph.

- (4) The valuer may, for the purposes of any assessment under [paragraph 68](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2026-03-16)—

- (a) enter onto land, and

- (b) make any reasonable request of the seller and landholder.

- (5) The valuer must, within the period of 6 weeks beginning with the day on which the valuer is appointed, give the seller and the landholder a notice in writing specifying the price payable by the landholder under [paragraph 68](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2026-03-16)[(9)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/9/2026-03-16) and setting out how the price was calculated.

- (6) The expenses of the valuer accrued in carrying out the valuer’s functions under [paragraph 68](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2026-03-16) and [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/69/2026-03-16) are to be—

- (a) met by the landholder, or

- (b) where [sub-paragraph (2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/67/2/2026-03-16) of [paragraph 67](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/67/2026-03-16) applies, shared equally between the landholders mentioned in that sub-paragraph.

- (7) The seller is liable to the landholder for any expenses met by the landholder by virtue of [sub-paragraph (6)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/69/6/2026-03-16) where—

- (a) the Land Court has made an order under [paragraph 66](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2026-03-16)[(8)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/8/2026-03-16),

- (b) the landholder to whom the order applies has complied with the order, and

- (c) the seller does not proceed with the sale of the land to the landholder.

- (8) The Scottish Ministers may by regulations make further provision for or in connection with the matters provided for in [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/69/2026-03-16) and [paragraphs 67](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/67/2026-03-16) and [68](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2026-03-16).

##### 70

- (1) The seller or the small landholder to whom a valuation carried out under [paragraph 68](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/68/2026-03-16) relates may appeal to the Lands Tribunal against the valuation.

- (2) An appeal under [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/70/2026-03-16) must—

- (a) state the grounds on which it is being made, and

- (b) be lodged within the period of 21 days beginning with the date of the notice under [paragraph 69](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/69/2026-03-16)[(5)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/69/5/2026-03-16).

- (3) In an appeal under [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/70/2026-03-16), the Lands Tribunal may—

- (a) reassess any value of the land (and any factor affecting the value) or of an estate (and how any reduction in the value of an estate is to be apportioned), and

- (b) for the purposes of [paragraph 66](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2026-03-16)[(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2/2026-03-16)[(b)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2/b/2026-03-16)[(ii)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2/b/ii/2026-03-16), determine the price.

- (4) The valuer whose valuation is appealed against may be a witness in the appeal proceedings.

- (5) In the appeal proceedings, in addition to the seller and the landholder, the following persons are entitled to be heard—

- (a) where the seller is—

- (i) a creditor in a standard security, the owner of the land,

- (ii) the owner of the land, any creditor in a standard security over the land or any part of it,

- (b) where the land forms part of an estate—

- (i) any creditor in a standard security over any other land forming part of the estate,

- (ii) any landholder, or other tenant, of any such land.

- (6) The Lands Tribunal is to give reasons for its decision on an appeal under [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/70/2026-03-16) and is to issue a written statement of these reasons.

- (7) The decision of the Lands Tribunal in an appeal under [this paragraph](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/70/2026-03-16) is final.

##### 71

- (1) This paragraph applies where, in an appeal before the Lands Tribunal under [paragraph 70](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/70/2026-03-16), an issue of law arises which may competently be determined by the Land Court by virtue of section 1(6) of the Scottish Land Court Act 1993 or this Act.

- (2) The Tribunal is to refer the issue to the Land Court for determination unless the Tribunal considers that it is not appropriate to do so.

##### 72

- (1) The Scottish Ministers may by regulations make provision for or in connection with the registration under [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/part/8/2026-03-16) of small landholders’ interests in buying the land comprised in their landholdings.

- (2) In particular (but without limit to that generality), regulations under [sub-paragraph (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/72/1/2026-03-16) may—

- (a) make provision about—

- (i) the manner in which a small landholder notifies the owner of the land of the landholder’s interest in buying the land,

- (ii) the procedure by which that interest is (or may be) registered,

- (iii) how an application for registration and entry in the Register may be challenged,

- (iv) the effect of registration,

- (v) the Keeper’s functions in respect of registration,

- (vi) the updating or correction of entries in the Register,

- (vii) the consequences of an application for registration, or an entry in the Register, being inaccurate in a material regard,

- (viii) the expiry or cancellation of an entry in the Register,

- (b) modify paragraphs [57](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/57/2026-03-16) to [63](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/63/2026-03-16),

- (c) if the Scottish Ministers consider it necessary or expedient, make consequential provision which modifies the other provisions in [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/part/8/2026-03-16).

- (3) Before laying a draft of a Scottish statutory instrument containing regulations under [sub-paragraph (1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/72/1/2026-03-16) before the Scottish Parliament, the Scottish Ministers must consult—

- (a) the Keeper,

- (b) such persons as the Scottish Ministers consider representative of the interests of small landholders and their landlords, and

- (c) such other persons as the Scottish Ministers consider are likely to have an interest in the registration of interests to buy land under [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/part/8/2026-03-16).

##### 73

In [this Part](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/part/8/2026-03-16)—

- “*eligible creditor*” has the meaning given by [paragraph 61](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/61/2026-03-16)[(6)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/61/6/2026-03-16),

- “*Keeper*” has the meaning given by [paragraph 57](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/57/2026-03-16)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/57/1/2026-03-16),

- “*notice of a proposal to transfer land*” means notice given under [paragraph 61](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/61/2026-03-16)[(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/61/2/2026-03-16),

- “*Register*” has the meaning given by [paragraph 57](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/57/2026-03-16)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/57/1/2026-03-16),

- “*seller*” has the meaning given by [paragraph 66](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2026-03-16)[(2)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2/2026-03-16)[(a)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/66/2/a/2026-03-16).

## Part 9 — Alternative dispute resolution

##### 74

- (1) Where this schedule makes provision for any matter to be determined by the Land Court, the matter may, if the landlord and small landholder agree at or after the time when the matter arises, instead be determined by another method of resolving the matter (including arbitration).

- (2) Sub-paragraph (1) does not apply in relation to any matter which may be determined by the Land Court—

- (a) in pursuance of—

- (i) paragraph 11(4) (whether a subsidiary or auxiliary purpose is reasonable and not inconsistent with the cultivation of the holding),

- (ii) any question or difference between the landlord and landholder arising in relation to Part 5 (disposal of holding by the landholder: renunciation, assignation or succession),

- (iii) any question or difference between the landlord and landholder arising in relation to Part 6 (removal of the landholder: breach of lease conditions, resumption by landlord),

- (iv) paragraph 84 (whether a term of a contract or agreement contracting out of a provision of this schedule is to be approved), or

- (b) on appeal.

##### 75

- (1) This paragraph applies to any arbitration to which a matter is referred by the landlord and small landholder under paragraph 74(1).

- (2) The agreement of the parties to refer the matter to arbitration has the effect of depriving each party of the right to—

- (a) have the matter heard (or any issue in relation to the matter determined) by the Land Court (other than on appeal), and

- (b) agree under paragraph 74(1) to another method of resolving the matter.

- (3) The landlord and landholder are to agree whether the arbitration is conducted by—

- (a) a single arbitrator, or

- (b) two arbitrators (with or without an overseer),

and the arbitrator or, as the case may be, each arbitrator, may be appointed by the parties or by a person nominated by them.

- (4) The procedure to be followed at arbitration (including any matters to be taken into account by the arbitrator and the matters to be contained in the award) are, subject to sub-paragraph (5), to be as the parties agree or, in the absence of such agreement, as the arbitrator considers appropriate.

- (5) Any provision of this schedule that would apply to the Land Court as respects its consideration or determination of any matter had the matter not been referred to arbitration applies as respects the consideration or determination of the matter by arbitration.

- (6) Any party to the arbitration may appeal to the Land Court against the arbitrator’s award on a question of law within 28 days of the award.

- (7) In an appeal under sub-paragraph (6) the Court may—

- (a) quash, confirm or vary the award or any part of it, and

- (b) where the Court quashes the award or any part of it—

- (i) remit the case to the arbitrator for further procedure, and

- (ii) direct the arbitrator on any question of law relevant to the case.

##### 76

- (1) Any person with an interest in a matter determined by an arbitration to which paragraph 75 applies that has reasonable grounds for believing that—

- (a) there has been material misconduct by the arbitrator, or

- (b) the arbitration has been improperly procured,

may make an application to the Land Court for an order under sub-paragraph (2).

- (2) Where, on such an application, the Land Court is satisfied that—

- (a) there has been material misconduct by the arbitrator, or the arbitration has been improperly procured, it may make an order setting aside the arbitrator’s award,

- (b) there has been material misconduct by the arbitrator, it may make an order removing the arbitrator.

> (14)
>   (1) The lease which gives rise to a statutory small tenancy becomes a lease of a small landholding if—
>     (a) not later than one month before the end of the period of the tenancy, the statutory small tenant gives the landlord written notice that the tenant wishes the lease to become a lease of a small landholding, and
>     (b) the landlord does not, before the expiry of the period of one month beginning with the day on which the notice is given, give the tenant a counter-notice stating that paragraph 27 of that schedule (in relation to rights to compensation for permanent improvements) is to apply as if the lease were a lease of a small landholding.
>   (2) Where a lease becomes a lease of a small landholding by virtue of subsection (1), it does so on the expiry of the period of the tenancy current when the notice mentioned in subsection (1)(a) is given.
>   (3) Where the landlord gives the tenant a counter-notice referred to in subsection (1)(b), paragraph 40 of schedule 2 of the Land Reform (Scotland) Act 2025 (in relation to rights to compensation for permanent improvements) applies to the lease of the statutory small tenancy as if the lease were a lease of a small landholding.

.

## Part 11 — General and interpretation

##### 84

Any term of a contract or agreement entered into by a small landholder purporting to deprive the small landholder of a right conferred on the small landholder by this schedule is void unless the contract or agreement is approved by the Land Court.

##### 85

Any term of—

- (a) a lease to which this schedule applies, or

- (b) any agreement in connection with such a lease (other than an agreement under [paragraph 74](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/74/2026-03-16)[(1)](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/paragraph/74/1/2026-03-16)),

that makes provision restricting any right of the landlord or small landholder to apply to the Land Court by virtue of this schedule to have a matter determined by the Court is, so far as it makes that provision, of no effect.

##### 86

In [this schedule](https://www.legislation.gov.uk/asp/2025/15/schedule/2/2026-03-16)—

- “*cultivation*” means the use of land for horticulture or husbandry and references to “cultivate” are to be construed accordingly,

- “*Land Court*” means the Scottish Land Court,

- “*Landholders Acts*” means the Small Landholders (Scotland) Acts 1886 to 1931,

- “*Lands Tribunal*” means the Lands Tribunal for Scotland,

- “*small landholder*” has the meaning given by paragraph 2(1),

- “*small landholding*” has the meaning given by paragraph 1(1).
